width:103.578ex; height:9.176ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       is the\n       <i>\n        angular momentum\n       </i>\n       , sometimes called, as here, the\n       <i>\n        moment of momentum\n       </i>\n       of the particle versus that particular center point. The equation\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              L\n             </mi>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mi>\n              r\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              m\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              v\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle L=rmv}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="L=rmv" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cae824c40f5d6282d0a4d286c1bdb7a7382c925e" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.95ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       combines a moment (a mass\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              m\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle m}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="m" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.051ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       turning moment arm\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              r\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle r}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.059ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       ) with a linear (straight-line equivalent) speed\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              v\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle v}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="v" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e07b00e7fc0847fbd16391c778d65bc25c452597" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.138ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       . Linear speed referred to the central point is simply the product of the distance\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              r\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle r}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.059ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       and the angular speed\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              \xcf\x89\n              <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\omega }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\omega " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/48eff443f9de7a985bb94ca3bde20813ea737be8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.456ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       versus the point:\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              v\n             </mi>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mi>\n              r\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              \xcf\x89\n              <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n             </mi>\n             <mo>\n              ,\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle v=r\\omega ,}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="v=r\\omega ," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/574eabd58d8470d1f1eded75c6b545fb35f48d5c" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:7.42ex; height:2.009ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       another moment. Hence, angular momentum contains a double moment:\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              L\n             </mi>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mi>\n              r\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              m\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              r\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              \xcf\x89\n              <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n             </mi>\n             <mo>\n              .\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle L=rmr\\omega .}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="L=rmr\\omega ." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e34e11145331181be5f931f586322cd5b0a81aee" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:10.985ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       Simplifying slightly,\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              L\n             </mi>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <msup>\n              <mi>\n               r\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mn>\n                2\n               </mn>\n              </mrow>\n             </msup>\n             <mi>\n              m\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              \xcf\x89\n              <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n             </mi>\n             <mo>\n              ,\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle L=r^{2}m\\omega ,}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="L=r^{2}m\\omega ," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d901cacb8e9e59ef9ac4d17913b6d7922c47808f" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.987ex; height:3.009ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       the quantity\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msup>\n              <mi>\n               r\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mn>\n                2\n               </mn>\n              </mrow>\n             </msup>\n             <mi>\n              m\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle r^{2}m}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="r^{2}m" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1bbbb15eaf46c7e295eefc1ceb32d90161f7bac4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.172ex; height:2.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       is the particle\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">\n        moment of inertia\n       </a>\n       , sometimes called the second moment of mass. It is a measure of rotational inertia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moment_of_inertia_examples.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Moment_of_inertia_examples.gif/220px-Moment_of_inertia_examples.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Moment_of_inertia_examples.gif/330px-Moment_of_inertia_examples.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Moment_of_inertia_examples.gif/440px-Moment_of_inertia_examples.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moment_of_inertia_examples.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">\n          Moment of inertia\n         </a>\n         (shown here), and therefore angular momentum, is different for every possible configuration of\n         <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">\n          mass\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Rotation_around_a_fixed_axis" title="Rotation around a fixed axis">\n          axis of rotation\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Because rotational inertia is a part of angular momentum, it necessarily includes all of the complications of\n       <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">\n        moment of inertia\n       </a>\n       , which is calculated by multiplying elementary bits of the mass by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Square_(algebra)" title="Square (algebra)">\n        squares\n       </a>\n       of their\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distances" title="Distances">\n        distances\n       </a>\n       from the center of rotation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oberg_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Oberg-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Therefore, the total moment of inertia, and the angular momentum, is a complex function of the configuration of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Matter" title="Matter">\n        matter\n       </a>\n       about the center of rotation and the orientation of the rotation for the various bits.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For a\n       <a href="/wiki/Rigid_body" title="Rigid body">\n        rigid body\n       </a>\n       , for instance a wheel or an asteroid, the orientation of rotation is simply the position of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rotation_around_a_fixed_axis" title="Rotation around a fixed axis">\n        rotation axis\n       </a>\n       versus the matter of the body. It may or may not pass through the\n       <a href="/wiki/Center_of_mass" title="Center of mass">\n        center of mass\n       </a>\n       , or it may lie completely outside of the body. For the same body, angular momentum may take a different value for every possible axis about which rotation may take place.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It reaches a minimum when the axis passes through the center of mass.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For a collection of objects revolving about a center, for instance all of the bodies of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">\n        Solar System\n       </a>\n       , the orientations may be somewhat organized, as is the Solar System, with most of the bodies\' axes lying close to the system\'s axis. Their orientations may also be completely random.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In brief, the more mass and the farther it is from the center of rotation (the longer the\n       <a href="/wiki/Torque#Moment_arm_formula" title="Torque">\n        moment arm\n       </a>\n       ), the greater the moment of inertia, and therefore the greater the angular momentum for a given\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">\n        angular velocity\n       </a>\n       . In many cases the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">\n        moment of inertia\n       </a>\n       , and hence the angular momentum, can be simplified by,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               I\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                k\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle k}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="k" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3c9a2c7b599b37105512c5d570edc034056dd40" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.222ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n        </span>\n        is the\n        <a href="/wiki/Radius_of_gyration" title="Radius of gyration">\n         radius of gyration\n        </a>\n        , the distance from the axis at which the entire mass\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math       m\n              </mi>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle m}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="m" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.051ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n        may be considered as concentrated.\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Similarly, for a\n       <a href="/wiki/Point_particle" title="Point particle">\n        point mass\n       </a>\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              m\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle m}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="m" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.051ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">\n        moment of inertia\n       </a>\n       is defined as,\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math          </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle I=r^{2}m}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="I=r^{2}m" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" </dd>\n       <dd>\n        where\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math the\n        <a href="/wiki/Radius" title="Radius">\n         radius\n        </a>\n        of the point mass from the center of rotation,\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       and for any collection of particles\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msub>\n </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="m_{i}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" sum,\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math           <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x91\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x91 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </munder>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                I\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <munder>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x91\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x91 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n _{i}r_{i}^{2}m_{i}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0e77d22473cf9495a86e27ee160fcfbd35b50253" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:17.433ex; height:5.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Angular momentum\'s dependence on position and shape is reflected in its\n       <a href="/wiki/Units_of_measurement" title="Units of measurement">\n        units\n       </a>\n       versus linear momentum:\n       <a href="/wiki/SI_derived_unit" title="SI derived unit">\n        kg\xc2\xb7m\n        <sup>\n         2\n        </sup>\n        /s\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/SI_derived_unit" title="SI derived unit">\n        N\xc2\xb7m\xc2\xb7s\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/SI_derived_unit" title="SI derived unit">\n        J\xc2\xb7s\n       </a>\n       for angular momentum versus\n       <a href="/wiki/SI_derived_unit" title="SI derived unit">\n        kg\xc2\xb7m/s\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/SI_derived_unit" title="SI derived unit">\n        N\xc2\xb7s\n       </a>\n       for linear momentum. Angular momentum\'s units can be interpreted as\n       <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">\n        torque\n       </a>\n       \xc2\xb7seconds,\n       <a href="/wiki/Work_(physics)" title="Work (physics)">\n        work\n       </a>\n       \xc2\xb7seconds, or\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       \xc2\xb7seconds. An object with angular momentum of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         L\n        </i>\n        N\xc2\xb7m\xc2\xb7s\n       </span>\n       can be reduced to zero rotation (all of the energy can be transferred out of it) by an angular\n       <a href="/wiki/Impulse_(physics)" title="Impulse (physics)">\n        impulse\n       </a>\n       of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         L\n        </i>\n        N\xc2\xb7m\xc2\xb7s\n       </span>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       or equivalently, by torque or work of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         L\n        </i>\n        N\xc2\xb7m\n       </span>\n       for one second, or energy of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         L\n        </i>\n        J\n       </span>\n       for one second.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Plane_(geometry)" title="Plane (geometry)">\n        plane\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Perpendicular" title="Perpendicular">\n        perpendicular\n       </a>\n       to the axis of angular momentum and passing through the center of mass\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is sometimes called the\n       <i>\n        invariable plane\n       </i>\n       , because the direction of the axis remains fixed if only the interactions of the bodies within the system, free from outside influences, are considered.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rankine_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Rankine-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One such plane is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Invariable_plane" title="Invariable plane">\n        invariable plane of the Solar System\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Angular_momentum_and_torque">\n        Angular momentum and torque\n       </span>\n Because angular acceleration is the time\n       <a href="/wiki/Derivative" title="Derivative">\n        derivative\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular -2.005ex; width:11.291ex; height:5.843ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display:      <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n               \xcf\x84\n               <!-- \xcf\x84 -->\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mi>\n              d\n             </mi>\n             <mi>\n              t\n             </mi>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mi>\n              d\n             </mi>\n             <mo stretchy="false">\n              (\n             </mo>\n             <mi>\n              I\n             </mi>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n               \xcf\x89\n               <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo stretchy="false">\n              )\n             </mo>\n             <mo>\n              ,\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\boldsymbol {\\tau }}dt=d(I{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}),}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\boldsymbol {\\tau }}dt=d(I{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }})," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/99cf0ac35493557e550afcf5610da8e31c8be8da" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.189ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       and integrating with respect to time,\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\xab\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\xab -->\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n                \xcf\x84\n                <!-- \xcf\x84 -->\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               t\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               I\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n                \xcf\x89\n                <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mtext>\n                constant\n               </mtext>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\int {\\boldsymbol {\\tau }}dt=I{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}+{\\text{constant}}.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="\\int {\\boldsymbol {\\tau }}dt=I{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}+{\\text{constant}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f69fcf137eb8e4e428f03f6d06afbc4d2c6fea30" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:24.326ex; height:5.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Therefore, a torque acting over time is equivalent to a change in angular momentum, known as\n       <i>\n        angular impulse\n       </i>\n       , by analogy with\n       <a href="/wiki/Impulse_(physics)" title="Impulse (physics)">\n        impulse\n       </a>\n       , which is defined as the change in\n       <a href="/wiki/Momentum" title="Momentum">\n        translational momentum\n       </a>\n       . The constant can be interpreted as the initial angular momentum of the body, before the torque began to act. In particular, if torque\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n               \xcf\x84\n               <!-- \xcf\x84 -->\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mn mathvariant="bold">\n               0\n              </mn>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              ,\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\boldsymbol {\\tau }}=\\mathbf {0} ,}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\boldsymbol {\\tau }}=\\mathbf {0} ," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b61f77c71a3b7a65d249195e0df1f9829c1b134b" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.542ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       then angular momentum\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               L\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mn mathvariant="bold">\n               0\n              </mn>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              +\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mtext>\n               constant\n              </mtext>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              .\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} =\\mathbf {0} +{\\text{constant}}.}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\mathbf {L} =\\mathbf {0} +{\\text{constant}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3ee8ffff6ff4a0528d17c6a75fd6af6b85463ed4" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:18.335ex; height:2.343ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       That is, if no torque acts upon a body, then its angular momentum remains constant. Conversely,\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                L\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               I\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n                \xcf\x89\n                <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} =I{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="\\mathbf {L} =I{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/794f5746b0089a4b7de0494195195a6291eda0aa" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.589ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       or Angular momentum =\n       <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">\n        moment of inertia\n       </a>\n       \xc3\x97\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">\n        angular velocity\n       </a>\n       , and its time\n       <a href="/wiki/Derivative" title="Derivative">\n        derivative\n       </a>\n       is\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mfrac>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  d\n                 </mi>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                   L\n                  </mi>\n                 </mrow>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  d\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi>\n                  t\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mfrac>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  d\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi>\n                  I\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  d\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi>\n                  t\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n                \xcf\x89\n                <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               I\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mfrac>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  d\n                 </mi>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n                   \xcf\x89\n                   <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n                  </mi>\n                 </mrow>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  d\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi>\n                  t\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle {\\frac {d\\mathbf {L} }{dt}}={\\frac {dI}{dt}}{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}+I{\\frac {d{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}}{dt}}.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\frac {d\\mathbf {L} }{dt}}={\\frac {dI}{dt}}{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}+I{\\frac {d{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}}{dt}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c5f27ba3006d0fb0890c5cc90543dd29e22c94c1" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:20.146ex; height:5.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Because moment of inertia is constant,\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mfrac>\n               <mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 d\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 I\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n               <mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 d\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 t\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </mfrac>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\frac {dI}{dt}}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\frac {dI}{dt}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/63a928856328237e006b28859b4d02228a2abdce" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:3.245ex; height:5.509ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       is zero, and\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mfrac>\n               <mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 d\n                </mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  L\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n               <mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 d\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 t\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </mfrac>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mn>\n              0\n             </mn>\n             <mo>\n              +\n             </mo>\n             <mi>\n              I\n             </mi>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mfrac>\n               <mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 d\n                </mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n                  \xcf\x89\n                  <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n               <mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 d\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 t\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </mfrac>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              ,\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\frac {d\\mathbf {L} }{dt}}=0+I{\\frac {d{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}}{dt}},}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\frac {d\\mathbf {L} }{dt}}=0+I{\\frac {d{\\boldsymbol {\\omega }}}{dt}}," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1ae5fb9bff67ab6a1f54a47bc3dfb6ba74a549d5" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:16.395ex; height:5.509ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       which, as above, reduces to\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mfrac>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  d\n                 </mi>\n                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                   L\n                  </mi>\n                 </mrow>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow>\n                 <mi>\n                  d\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi>\n                  t\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               I\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n                \xce\xb1\n                <!-- \xce\xb1 -->\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle {\\frac {d\\mathbf {L} }{dt}}=I{\\boldsymbol {\\alpha }}.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\frac {d\\mathbf {L} }{dt}}=I{\\boldsymbol {\\alpha }}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9a2689e86f588ad8b3d53bbcc3481cfd1e6d14c1" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:10.409ex; height:5.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Therefore, the time rate of change of angular momentum about a particular center of rotation is equivalent to applied\n       <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">\n        torque\n       </a>\n       about that center.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taylor90_4-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Taylor90-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       If angular momentum is constant,\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mfrac>\n               <mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 d\n                </mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  L\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n               <mrow>\n                <mi>\n                 d\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 t\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </mfrac>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mn>\n              0\n             </mn>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\frac {d\\mathbf {L} }{dt}}=0}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\frac {d\\mathbf {L} }{dt}}=0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9d7f52e22493a31877db469d39a8fef077d4f9a1" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:7.963ex; height:5.509ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       and no torque is applied.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_of_angular_momentum">\n        Conservation of angular momentum\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Conservation of angular momentum">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cup_of_Russia_2010_-_Yuko_Kawaguti_(2).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="307" height="358" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Cup_of_Russia_2010_-_Yuko_Kawaguti_%282%29.jpg/220px-Cup_of_Russia_2010_-_Yuko_Kawaguti_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/68/Cup_of_Russia_2010_-_Yuko_Kawaguti_%282%29.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cup_of_Russia_2010_-_Yuko_Kawaguti_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">\n          figure skater\n         </a>\n         conserves angular momentum \xe2\x80\x93 her\n         <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">\n          rotational speed\n         </a>\n         increases as her\n         <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">\n          moment of inertia\n         </a>\n         decreases by drawing in her arms and legs.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A rotational analog of\n       <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion#Newton.27s_third_law" title="Newton\'s laws of motion">\n        Newton\'s Third Law of Motion\n       </a>\n       might be written, "In a\n       <a href="/wiki/Closed_system" title="Closed system">\n        closed system\n       </a>\n       , no torque can be exerted on any matter without the exertion on some other matter of an equal and opposite torque."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crew_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Crew-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hence,\n       <i>\n        angular momentum can be exchanged between objects in a closed system, but total angular momentum before and after an exchange remains constant (is conserved).\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Similarly, a rotational analog of\n       <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion#Newton.27s_second_law" title="Newton\'s laws of motion">\n        Newton\'s Second law of Motion\n       </a>\n       might be, "A change in angular momentum is proportional to the applied torque and occurs about the same axis as that torque."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crew_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Crew-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since a torque applied over time is equivalent to a change in angular momentum, then if torque is zero, angular momentum is constant. As above, a system with constant angular momentum is a closed system. Therefore,\n       <i>\n        requiring the system to be closed is equivalent to requiring that no external influence, in the form of a torque, acts upon it.\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A rotational analog of\n       <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion#Newton.27s_first_law" title="Newton\'s laws of motion">\n        Newton\'s First Law of Motion\n       </a>\n       might be written, "A body continues in a state of rest or of uniform rotation unless acted by an external torque."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Crew_18-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Crew-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Thus\n       <i>\n        with no external influence to act upon it, the original angular momentum of the system is conserved\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The conservation of angular momentum is used in analyzing\n       <a href="/wiki/Classical_central-force_problem" title="Classical central-force problem">\n        <i>\n         central force motion\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       . If the net force on some body is directed always toward some point, the\n       <i>\n        center\n       </i>\n       , then there is no torque on the body with respect to the center, as all of the force is directed along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Position_(vector)" title="Position (vector)">\n        radius vector\n       </a>\n       , and none is\n       <a href="/wiki/Perpendicular" title="Perpendicular">\n        perpendicular\n       </a>\n       to the radius. Mathematically, torque\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold-italic">\n               \xcf\x84\n               <!-- \xcf\x84 -->\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               r\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              \xc3\x97\n              <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               F\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mn mathvariant="bold">\n               0\n              </mn>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              ,\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\boldsymbol {\\tau }}=\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {F} =\\mathbf {0} ,}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\boldsymbol {\\tau }}=\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {F} =\\mathbf {0} ," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bce23213f7078a404609088e6b314db820290527" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:15.307ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       because in this case\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               r\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {r} }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\mathbf {r} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/eca0f46511c4c986c48b254073732c0bd98ae0c1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.113ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               F\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {F} }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\mathbf {F} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/da18bef8c979f3548bb0d8976f5844012d7b8256" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.693ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       are parallel vectors. Therefore, the angular momentum of the body about the center is constant. This is the case with\n       <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">\n        gravitational attraction\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">\n        orbits\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planets\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">\n        satellites\n       </a>\n       , where the gravitational force is always directed toward the primary body and orbiting bodies conserve angular momentum by exchanging distance and velocity as they move about the primary. Central force motion is also used in the analysis of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bohr_model" title="Bohr model">\n        Bohr model\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atom" title="Atom">\n        atom\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For a planet, angular momentum is distributed between the spin of the planet and its revolution in its orbit, and these are often exchanged by various mechanisms. The conservation of angular momentum in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_theory" title="Lunar theory">\n        Earth\xe2\x80\x93Moon system\n       </a>\n       results in the transfer of angular momentum from Earth to Moon, due to\n       <a href="/wiki/Tidal_acceleration" title="Tidal acceleration">\n        tidal torque\n       </a>\n       the Moon exerts on the Earth. This in turn results in the slowing down of the rotation rate of Earth, at about 65.7 nanoseconds per day,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in gradual increase of the radius of Moon\'s orbit, at about 3.82\xc2\xa0centimeters per year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PrecessionOfATop.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="300" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/PrecessionOfATop.svg/250px-PrecessionOfATop.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/PrecessionOfATop.svg/375px-PrecessionOfATop.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/PrecessionOfATop.svg/500px-PrecessionOfATop.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PrecessionOfATop.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">\n          torque\n         </a>\n         caused by the two opposing forces\n         <b>\n          F\n         </b>\n         <sub>\n          g\n         </sub>\n         and \xe2\x88\x92\n         <b>\n          F\n         </b>\n         <sub>\n          g\n         </sub>\n         causes a change in the angular momentum\n         <b>\n          L\n         </b>\n         in the direction of that torque (since torque is the time derivative of angular momentum). This causes the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spinning_top" title="Spinning top">\n          top\n         </a>\n         to\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precess" title="Precess">\n          precess\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The conservation of angular momentum explains the angular acceleration of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice_skating" title="Ice skating">\n        ice skater\n       </a>\n       as she brings her arms and legs close to the vertical axis of rotation. By bringing part of the mass of her body closer to the axis she decreases her body\'s moment of inertia. Because angular momentum is the product of\n       <a href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia" title="Moment of inertia">\n        moment of inertia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">\n        angular velocity\n       </a>\n       , if the angular momentum remains constant (is conserved), then the angular velocity (rotational speed) of the skater must increase.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The same phenomenon results in extremely fast spin of compact stars (like\n       <a href="/wiki/White_dwarf" title="White dwarf">\n        white dwarfs\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Neutron_star" title="Neutron star">\n        neutron stars\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">\n        black holes\n       </a>\n       ) when they are formed out of much larger and slower rotating stars. Decrease in the size of an object\n       <i>\n        n\n       </i>\n       times results in increase of its angular velocity by the factor of\n       <i>\n        n\n       </i>\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Conservation is not always a full explanation for the dynamics of a system but is a key constraint. For example, a spinning\n       <a href="/wiki/Top" title="Top">\n        top\n       </a>\n       is subject to gravitational torque making it lean over and change the angular momentum about the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nutation" title="Nutation">\n        nutation\n       </a>\n       axis, but neglecting friction at the point of spinning contact, it has a conserved angular momentum about its spinning axis, and another about its\n       <a href="/wiki/Precession" title="Precession">\n        precession\n       </a>\n       axis. Also, in any\n       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_system" title="Planetary system">\n        planetary system\n       </a>\n       , the planets, star(s), comets, and asteroids can all move in numerous complicated ways, but only so that the angular momentum of the system is conserved.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Noether%27s_theorem" title="Noether\'s theorem">\n        Noether\'s theorem\n       </a>\n       states that every\n       <a href="/wiki/Conservation_law" title="Conservation law">\n        conservation law\n       </a>\n       is associated with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Symmetry" title="Symmetry">\n        symmetry\n       </a>\n       (invariant) of the underlying physics. The symmetry associated with conservation of angular momentum is\n       <a href="/wiki/Rotational_invariance" title="Rotational invariance">\n        rotational invariance\n       </a>\n       . The fact that the physics of a system is unchanged if it is rotated by any angle about an axis implies that angular momentum is conserved.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Angular_momentum_in_orbital_mechanics">\n        Angular momentum in orbital mechanics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Angular momentum in orbital mechanics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Specific_relative_angular_momentum" title="Specific relative angular momentum">\n        Specific relative angular momentum\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In astrodynamics and\n       <a href="/wiki/Celestial_mechanics" title="Celestial mechanics">\n        celestial mechanics\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <i>\n        massless\n       </i>\n       (or\n       <i>\n        per unit mass\n       </i>\n       ) angular momentum is defined\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                h\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                r\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               \xc3\x97\n               <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                v\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {h} =\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {v} ,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="\\mathbf {h} =\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {v} ," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6d21943fd68a6ac77006c0d7b71cedd7b3639b10" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.647ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       called\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Specific_relative_angular_momentum" title="Specific relative angular momentum">\n         specific angular momentum\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . Note that\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               L\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mi>\n              m\n             </mi>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               h\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              .\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} =m\\mathbf {h} .}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\mathbf {L} =m\\mathbf {h} ." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/451a7af5aa41456418306ab6657c780e020a4855" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.932ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">\n        Mass\n       </a>\n       is often unimportant in orbital mechanics calculations, because motion is defined by\n       <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">\n        gravity\n       </a>\n       . The primary body of the system is often so much larger than any bodies in motion about it that the smaller bodies have a negligible gravitational effect on it; it is, in effect, stationary. All bodies are apparently attracted by its gravity in the same way, regardless of mass, and therefore all move approximately the same way under the same conditions.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Solid_bodies">\n        Solid bodies\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Solid bodies">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       For a continuous mass distribution with\n       <a href="/wiki/Density" title="Density">\n        density\n       </a>\n       function\n       <i>\n        \xcf\x81\n       </i>\n       (\n       <b>\n        r\n       </b>\n       ), a differential\n       <a href="/wiki/Volume_element" title="Volume element">\n        volume element\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        dV\n       </i>\n       with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Position_vector" title="Position vector">\n        position vector\n       </a>\n       <b>\n        r\n       </b>\n       within the mass has a mass element\n       <i>\n        dm\n       </i>\n       =\n       <i>\n        \xcf\x81\n       </i>\n       (\n       <b>\n        r\n       </b>\n       )\n       <i>\n        dV\n       </i>\n       . Therefore, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Infinitesimal" title="Infinitesimal">\n        infinitesimal\n       </a>\n       angular momentum of this element is:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n         </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                r\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mrow </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Volume_integral" title="Volume integral">\n        integrating\n       </a>\n       this\n       <a href="/wiki/Differential_(infinitesimal)" title="Differential (infinitesimal)">\n        differential\n       </a>\n       over the volume of the entire mass gives its total angular momentum:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math       <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xcf\x81\n               <!-- \xcf\x81 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n {r} )\\mathbf {v} }\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="\\mathbf {L} =\\int _{V}dV\\mathbf {r} \\times \\rho (\\mathbf {r} )\\mathbf {v} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0dfcf143a296d05052ee9f5612c8c78977806eea" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:20.485ex; height:5.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       In the derivation which follows, integrals similar to this can replace the sums for the case of continuous mass.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Collection_of_particles">\n        Collection of particles\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n <i>\n          i\n         </i>\n         is the sum of the cross products\n         <b>\n          R\n         </b>\n         \xc3\x97\n         <i>\n          M\n         </i>\n         <b>\n .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       For a collection of particles in motion about an arbitrary origin, it is informative to develop the equation of angular momentum by resolving their motion into components about their own center of mass and about the origin. Similar to\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum#Single_particle" title="Angular momentum">\n        <b>\n         Single particle\n        </b>\n       </a>\n       , below, it is the angular momentum of one particle of mass\n       <i>\n        M\n       </i>\n       at the center of mass moving with velocity\n       <b>\n        V\n       </b>\n       . The second term is the angular momentum of the particles moving relative to the center of mass, similar to\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum#Fixed_center_of_mass" title="Angular momentum">\n        <b>\n         Fixed center of mass\n        </b>\n       </a>\n       , below. The result is general \xe2\x80\x94 the motion of the particles is not restricted to rotation or revolution about the origin or center of mass. The particles need not be individual masses, but can be elements of a continuous distribution, such as a solid body.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Rearranging equation (\n       <b>\n        <a </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </munder>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                I\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <msub>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span id="Angular_momentum_(modern_definition)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Angular_momentum_.28modern_definition.29">\n        Angular momentum (modern definition)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Angular momentum (modern definition)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angular_momentum_bivector_and_pseudovector.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="239" data-file-width="350" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Angular_momentum_bivector_and_pseudovector.svg/275px-Angular_momentum_bivector_and_pseudovector.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Angular_momentum_bivector_and_pseudovector.svg/413px-Angular_momentum_bivector_and_pseudovector.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Angular_momentum_bivector_and_pseudovector.svg/550px-Angular_momentum_bivector_and_pseudovector.svg.png 2x" width="275"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angular_momentum_bivector_and_pseudovector.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The 3-angular momentum as a\n         <a href="/wiki/Bivector" title="Bivector">\n          bivector\n         </a>\n         (plane element) and\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axial_vector" title="Axial vector">\n          axial vector\n         </a>\n         , of a particle of mass\n         <i>\n          m\n         </i>\n         with instantaneous 3-position\n         <b>\n          x\n         </b>\n         and 3-momentum\n         <b>\n          p\n         </b>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In modern (20th century) theoretical physics, angular momentum (not including any intrinsic angular momentum \xe2\x80\x93 see\n       <a href="#Angular_momentum_in_quantum_mechanics">\n        below\n       </a>\n       ) is described using a different formalism, instead of a classical\n       <a href="/wiki/Pseudovector" title="Pseudovector">\n        pseudovector\n       </a>\n       . In this formalism, angular momentum is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2-form" title="2-form">\n        2-form\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Noether_charge" title="Noether charge">\n        Noether charge\n       </a>\n       associated with rotational invariance. As a result, angular momentum is not conserved for general\n       <a href="/wiki/Curved_space" title="Curved space">\n        curved spacetimes\n       </a>\n       , unless it happens to be asymptotically rotationally invariant.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In classical mechanics, the angular momentum of a particle can be reinterpreted as a plane element:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                L\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                r\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\xa7\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\xa7 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                p\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} =\\mathbf {r} \\wedge \\mathbf {p} \\,,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="\\mathbf {L} =\\mathbf {r} \\wedge \\mathbf {p} \\,," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a728ebb909aecdf46e42d9d76e7ef344fa0bf0ba" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.973ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       in which the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exterior_product" title="Exterior product">\n        exterior product\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x88\xa7 replaces the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cross_product" title="Cross product">\n        cross product\n       </a>\n       \xc3\x97 (these products have similar characteristics but are nonequivalent). This has the advantage of a clearer geometric interpretation as a plane element, defined from the\n       <b>\n        x\n       </b>\n       and\n       <b>\n        p\n       </b>\n       vectors, and the expression is true in any number of dimensions (two or higher). In Cartesian coordinates:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n           +\n                  </mo>\n                  <msub>\n                   <mi>\n                    L\n                   </mi>\n                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                    <mi>\n                     y\n                    </mi>\n                    <mi>\n                     z\n                    </mi>\n                   </mrow>\n                  </msub>\n                  <msub>\n                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                    <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                     e\n                    </mi>\n                   </mrow>\n width:70.527ex; height:6.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       or more compactly in index notation:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 j\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                x\n               </mi>\n               <mrow
