encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle L_{ij}=x_{i}p_{j}-x_{j}p_{i}\\,.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="L_{ij}=x_{i}p_{j}-x_{j}p_{i}\\,." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/32e4099346e97f23ae25a0c5424c77bfeaa02cce" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:18.578ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The angular velocity can also be defined as an antisymmetric second order tensor, with components\n       <i>\n        \xcf\x89\n        <sub>\n         ij\n        </sub>\n       </i>\n       . The relation between the two antisymmetric tensors is given by the moment of inertia which must now be a fourth order tensor:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                L\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 j\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                I\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 j\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 k\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 \xe2\x84\x93\n                 <!-- \xe2\x84\x93 -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                \xcf\x89\n                <!-- \xcf\x89 -->\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 k\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 \xe2\x84\x93\n                 <!-- \xe2\x84\x93 -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle L_{ij}=I_{ijk\\ell }\\omega _{k\\ell }\\,.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="L_{ij}=I_{ijk\\ell }\\omega _{k\\ell }\\,." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/34c1df7926b52a248cb20e1277546a850aec2045" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:14.566ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Again, this equation in\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       and\n       <b>\n        \xcf\x89\n       </b>\n       as tensors is true in any number of dimensions. This equation also appears in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Geometric_algebra" title="Geometric algebra">\n        geometric algebra\n       </a>\n       formalism, in which\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       and\n       <b>\n        \xcf\x89\n       </b>\n       are bivectors, and the moment of inertia is a mapping between them.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Relativistic_mechanics" title="Relativistic mechanics">\n        relativistic mechanics\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Relativistic_angular_momentum" title="Relativistic angular momentum">\n        relativistic angular momentum\n       </a>\n       of a particle is expressed as an\n       <a href="/wiki/Antisymmetric_tensor" title="Antisymmetric tensor">\n        antisymmetric tensor\n       </a>\n       of second order:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                M\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xb1\n                 <!-- \xce\xb1 -->\n                </mi>\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xb2\n                 <!-- \xce\xb2 -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                X\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xb1\n                 <!-- \xce\xb1 -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mtext>\n              </mtext>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                P\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xb2\n                 <!-- \xce\xb2 -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                X\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xb2\n                 <!-- \xce\xb2 -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                P\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 \xce\xb1\n                 <!-- \xce\xb1 -->\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle M_{\\alpha \\beta }=X_{\\alpha }\\ P_{\\beta }-X_{\\beta }P_{\\alpha }}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="M_{\\alpha \\beta }=X_{\\alpha }\\ P_{\\beta }-X_{\\beta }P_{\\alpha }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/33775f6e0e225621463164e55556ac213a780617" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:22.867ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       in the language of\n       <a href="/wiki/Four-vector" title="Four-vector">\n        four-vectors\n       </a>\n       , namely the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four-position" title="Four-position">\n        four position\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        X\n       </i>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four_momentum" title="Four momentum">\n        four momentum\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        P\n       </i>\n       , and absorbs the above\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       together with the motion of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre_of_mass" title="Centre of mass">\n        centre of mass\n       </a>\n       of the particle.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In each of the above cases, for a system of particles, the total angular momentum is just the sum of the individual particle angular momenta, and the centre of mass is for the system.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Angular_momentum_in_quantum_mechanics">\n        Angular momentum in quantum mechanics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Angular momentum in quantum mechanics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum_operator" title="Angular momentum operator">\n        Angular momentum operator\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Angular momentum in\n       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">\n        quantum mechanics\n       </a>\n       differs in many profound respects from angular momentum in\n       <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">\n        classical mechanics\n       </a>\n       . In\n       <a href="/wiki/Relativistic_quantum_mechanics#Relativistic_quantum_angular_momentum" title="Relativistic quantum mechanics">\n        relativistic quantum mechanics\n       </a>\n       , it differs even more, in which the above relativistic definition becomes a tensorial operator.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Spin,_orbital,_and_total_angular_momentum">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spin.2C_orbital.2C_and_total_angular_momentum">\n        Spin, orbital, and total angular momentum\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Spin, orbital, and total angular momentum">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Spin_(physics)" title="Spin (physics)">\n        Spin (physics)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Classical_angular_momentum.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="527" data-file-width="666" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Classical_angular_momentum.svg/350px-Classical_angular_momentum.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Classical_angular_momentum.svg/525px-Classical_angular_momentum.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Classical_angular_momentum.svg/700px-Classical_angular_momentum.svg.png 2x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Classical_angular_momentum.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Angular momenta of a\n         <i>\n          classical\n         </i>\n         object.\n         <br/>\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          Left:\n         </b>\n         "spin" angular momentum\n         <b>\n          S\n         </b>\n         is really orbital angular momentum of the object at every point,\n         <br/>\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          right:\n         </b>\n         extrinsic orbital angular momentum\n         <b>\n          L\n         </b>\n         about an axis,\n         <br/>\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          top:\n         </b>\n         the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moment_of_inertia_tensor" title="Moment of inertia tensor">\n          moment of inertia tensor\n         </a>\n         <b>\n          I\n         </b>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Angular_velocity" title="Angular velocity">\n          angular velocity\n         </a>\n         <b>\n          \xcf\x89\n         </b>\n         (\n         <b>\n          L\n         </b>\n         is not always parallel to\n         <b>\n          \xcf\x89\n         </b>\n         ),\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n          <a href="#cite_note-29">\n           [29]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <br/>\n         <br/>\n         <b>\n          bottom:\n         </b>\n         momentum\n         <b>\n          p\n         </b>\n         and its radial position\n         <b>\n          r\n         </b>\n         from the axis.The total angular momentum (spin plus orbital) is\n         <b>\n          J\n         </b>\n         . For a\n         <i>\n          quantum\n         </i>\n         particle the interpretations are different;\n         <a href="/wiki/Spin_(physics)" title="Spin (physics)">\n          particle spin\n         </a>\n         does\n         <i>\n          not\n         </i>\n         have the above interpretation.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The classical definition of angular momentum as\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               L\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               r\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              \xc3\x97\n              <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               p\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} =\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {p} }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\mathbf {L} =\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {p} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/22179a9b81408e19de312b5fbfec30ff62cefa4a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.187ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       can be carried over to quantum mechanics, by reinterpreting\n       <b>\n        r\n       </b>\n       as the quantum\n       <a href="/wiki/Position_operator" title="Position operator">\n        position operator\n       </a>\n       and\n       <b>\n        p\n       </b>\n       as the quantum\n       <a href="/wiki/Momentum_operator" title="Momentum operator">\n        momentum operator\n       </a>\n       .\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       is then an\n       <a href="/wiki/Operator_(physics)" title="Operator (physics)">\n        operator\n       </a>\n       , specifically called the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum_operator" title="Angular momentum operator">\n         orbital angular momentum operator\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . The components of the angular momentum operator satisfy the commutation relations of the Lie algebra so(3) of the rotation group SO(3). Indeed, these operators are precisely the infinitesimal action of the rotation group on the quantum Hilbert space.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (See also the discussion below of the angular momentum operators as the generators of rotations.)\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       However, in quantum physics, there is another type of angular momentum, called\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Spin_(physics)" title="Spin (physics)">\n         spin angular momentum\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , represented by the spin operator\n       <b>\n        S\n       </b>\n       . Almost all\n       <a href="/wiki/Elementary_particle" title="Elementary particle">\n        elementary particles\n       </a>\n       have spin. Spin is often depicted as a particle literally spinning around an axis, but this is a misleading and inaccurate picture: spin is an intrinsic property of a particle, unrelated to any sort of motion in space and fundamentally different from orbital angular momentum. All\n       <a href="/wiki/Elementary_particle" title="Elementary particle">\n        elementary particles\n       </a>\n       have a characteristic spin, for example\n       <a href="/wiki/Electron" title="Electron">\n        electrons\n       </a>\n       have "spin 1/2" (this actually means "spin\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reduced_Planck_constant" title="Reduced Planck constant">\n        \xc4\xa7\n       </a>\n       /2") while\n       <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">\n        photons\n       </a>\n       have "spin 1" (this actually means "spin \xc4\xa7").\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Finally, there is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Total_angular_momentum" title="Total angular momentum">\n        total angular momentum\n       </a>\n       <b>\n        J\n       </b>\n       , which combines both the spin and orbital angular momentum of all particles and fields. (For one particle,\n       <b>\n        J\n       </b>\n       =\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       +\n       <b>\n        S\n       </b>\n       .)\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservation_of_angular_momentum" title="Conservation of angular momentum">\n        Conservation of angular momentum\n       </a>\n       applies to\n       <b>\n        J\n       </b>\n       , but not to\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       or\n       <b>\n        S\n       </b>\n       ; for example, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spin%E2%80%93orbit_interaction" title="Spin\xe2\x80\x93orbit interaction">\n        spin\xe2\x80\x93orbit interaction\n       </a>\n       allows angular momentum to transfer back and forth between\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       and\n       <b>\n        S\n       </b>\n       , with the total remaining constant. Electrons and photons need not have integer-based values for total angular momentum, but can also have fractional values.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Quantization">\n        Quantization\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Quantization">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">\n        quantum mechanics\n       </a>\n       , angular momentum is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angular_momentum_quantization" title="Angular momentum quantization">\n        quantized\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 that is, it cannot vary continuously, but only in "\n       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_number" title="Quantum number">\n        quantum leaps\n       </a>\n       " between certain allowed values. For any system, the following restrictions on measurement results apply, where\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" width:1.317ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reduced_Planck_constant" title="Reduced Planck constant">\n        reduced Planck constant\n       </a>\n       and\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Circular_Standing_Wave.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="279" data-file-width="295" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Circular_Standing_Wave.gif/220px-Circular_Standing_Wave.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Circular_Standing_Wave.gif 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Circular_Standing_Wave.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         In this\n         <a href="/wiki/Standing_wave" title="Standing wave">\n          standing wave\n         </a>\n         on a circular string, the circle is broken into exactly 8\n         <a href="/wiki/Wavelength" title="Wavelength">\n          wavelengths\n         </a>\n         . A standing wave like this can have 0,1,2, or any integer number of wavelengths around the circle, but it\n         <i>\n          cannot\n         </i>\n         have a non-integer number of wavelengths like 8.3. In quantum mechanics, angular momentum is quantized for a similar reason.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       (There are additional restrictions as well, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum_operator" title="Angular momentum operator">\n        angular momentum operator\n       </a>\n       for details.)\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reduced_Planck_constant" title="Reduced Planck constant">\n        reduced Planck constant\n       </a>\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi class="MJX-variant">\n              \xe2\x84\x8f\n              <!-- \xe2\x84\x8f -->\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\hbar }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\hbar " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/de68de3a92517953436c93b5a76461d49160cc41" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.317ex; height:2.176ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       is tiny by everyday standards, about 10\n       <sup>\n        \xe2\x88\x9234\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Joule-second" title="Joule-second">\n        J s\n       </a>\n       , and therefore this quantization does not noticeably affect the angular momentum of macroscopic objects. However, it is very important in the microscopic world. For example, the structure of\n       <a href="/wiki/Electron_shell" title="Electron shell">\n        electron shells\n       </a>\n       and subshells in chemistry is significantly affected by the quantization of angular momentum.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Quantization of angular momentum was first postulated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Niels_Bohr" title="Niels Bohr">\n        Niels Bohr\n       </a>\n       in his\n       <a href="/wiki/Bohr_model" title="Bohr model">\n        Bohr model\n       </a>\n       of the atom and was later predicted by\n       <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Schr%C3%B6dinger" title="Erwin Schr\xc3\xb6dinger">\n        Erwin Schr\xc3\xb6dinger\n       </a>\n       in his\n       <a href="/wiki/Schr%C3%B6dinger_equation#Quantization" title="Schr\xc3\xb6dinger equation">\n        Schr\xc3\xb6dinger equation\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Uncertainty">\n        Uncertainty\n      </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In the definition\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle p_{y}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="p_{y}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1108b3eff778ca6f026e3e28c26cb093174cc2d0" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; margin-left: -0.079ex; width:2.316ex; height:2.343ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                z\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle p_{z}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="p_{z}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1dbd3c1a6173a7974e0095301da94447c5f67657" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.079ex; width:2.268ex; height:2.009ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       . However, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Uncertainty_principle" title="Uncertainty principle">\n        Heisenberg uncertainty principle\n       </a>\n       tells us that it is not possible for all six of these quantities to be known simultaneously with arbitrary precision. Therefore, there are limits to what can be known or measured about a particle\'s angular momentum. It turns out that the best that one can do is to simultaneously measure both the angular momentum vector\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnitude_(vector)" title="Magnitude (vector)">\n        magnitude\n       </a>\n       and its component along one axis.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The uncertainty is closely related to the fact that different components of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum_operator" title="Angular momentum operator">\n        angular momentum operator\n       </a>\n       do not\n       <a href="/wiki/Commutator" title="Commutator">\n        commute\n       </a>\n       , for example\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               L\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                x\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               L\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                y\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <mo>\n              \xe2\x89\xa0\n              <!-- \xe2\x89\xa0 -->\n             </mo>\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               L\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                y\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n             <msub>\n              <mi>\n               L\n              </mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi>\n                x\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n             </msub>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle L_{x}L_{y}\\neq L_{y}L_{x}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="L_{x}L_{y}\\neq L_{y}L_{x}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/14b5e35b0c4b63f2a2bd24c39f08e6e1c86f9528" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:13.955ex; height:3.009ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       . (For the precise\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commutation_relation" title="Commutation relation">\n        commutation relations\n       </a>\n       , see\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum_operator" title="Angular momentum operator">\n        angular momentum operator\n       </a>\n       .)\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Total_angular_momentum_as_generator_of_rotations">\n        Total angular momentum as generator of rotations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Total angular momentum as generator of rotations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As mentioned above, orbital angular momentum\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       is defined as in classical mechanics:\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               L\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              =\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               r\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              \xc3\x97\n              <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               p\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} =\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {p} }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\mathbf {L} =\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {p} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/22179a9b81408e19de312b5fbfec30ff62cefa4a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.187ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       , but\n       <i>\n        total\n       </i>\n       angular momentum\n       <b>\n        J\n       </b>\n       is defined in a different, more basic way:\n       <b>\n        J\n       </b>\n       is defined as the "generator of rotations".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-littlejohn_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-littlejohn-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       More specifically,\n       <b>\n        J\n       </b>\n       is defined so that the operator\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               R\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mover>\n                 <mi>\n                  n\n                 </mi>\n                 <mo stretchy="false">\n                  ^\n                  <!-- ^ -->\n                 </mo>\n                </mover>\n               </mrow>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xcf\x95\n               <!-- \xcf\x95 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x89\xa1\n               <!-- \xe2\x89\xa1 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               exp\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x81\xa1\n               <!-- \xe2\x81\xa1 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mrow>\n               <mo>\n                (\n               </mo>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x92\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mfrac>\n                 <mi>\n                  i\n                 </mi>\n                 <mi class="MJX-variant">\n                  \xe2\x84\x8f\n                  <!-- \xe2\x84\x8f -->\n                 </mi>\n                </mfrac>\n               </mrow>\n               <mi>\n                \xcf\x95\n                <!-- \xcf\x95 -->\n               </mi>\n               <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n               </mspace>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                 J\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x8b\x85\n                <!-- \xe2\x8b\x85 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mover>\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                   <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                    n\n                   </mi>\n                  </mrow>\n                  <mo stretchy="false">\n                   ^\n                   <!-- ^ -->\n                  </mo>\n                 </mover>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n               <mo>\n                )\n               </mo>\n              </mrow>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle R({\\hat {n}},\\phi )\\equiv \\exp \\left(-{\\frac {i}{\\hbar }}\\phi \\,\\mathbf {J} \\cdot {\\hat {\\mathbf {n} }}\\right)}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="R({\\hat {n}},\\phi )\\equiv \\exp \\left(-{\\frac {i}{\\hbar }}\\phi </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rotation_operator_(quantum_mechanics)" title="Rotation operator (quantum mechanics)">\n        rotation operator\n       </a>\n       that takes any system and rotates it by angle\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mi>\n              \xcf\x95\n              <!-- \xcf\x95 -->\n             </mi>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\phi }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\phi " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/72b1f30316670aee6270a28334bdf4f5072cdde4" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.396ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       about the axis\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mover>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  n\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n                <mo stretchy="false">\n                 ^\n                 <!-- ^ -->\n                </mo>\n               </mover>\n              </mrow>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {\\hat {\\mathbf {n} }}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\hat {\\mathbf {n} }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/aae87b164ba005e99b51066c46d1eacc7f56564a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.496ex; height:2.343ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       . (The "exp" in the formula refers to\n       <a href="/wiki/Matrix_exponential" title="Matrix exponential">\n        operator exponential\n       </a>\n       ) To put this the other way around, whatever our quantum Hilbert space is, we expect that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rotation_group_SO(3)" title="Rotation group SO(3)">\n        rotation group SO(3)\n       </a>\n       will act on it. There is then an associated action of the Lie algebra so(3) of SO(3); the operators describing the action of so(3) on our Hilbert space are the (total) angular momentum operators.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The relationship between the angular momentum operator and the rotation operators is the same as the relationship between\n       <a href="/wiki/Lie_algebra" title="Lie algebra">\n        Lie algebras\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lie_group" title="Lie group">\n        Lie groups\n       </a>\n       in mathematics. The close relationship between angular momentum and rotations is reflected in\n       <a href="/wiki/Noether%27s_theorem" title="Noether\'s theorem">\n        Noether\'s theorem\n       </a>\n       that proves that angular momentum is conserved whenever the laws of physics are rotationally invariant.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Angular_momentum_in_electrodynamics">\n        Angular momentum in electrodynamics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Angular momentum in electrodynamics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Momentum#Particle_in_field" title="Momentum">\n        Momentum (Particle in field)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       When describing the motion of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Charged_particle" title="Charged particle">\n        charged particle\n       </a>\n       in an\n       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_field" title="Electromagnetic field">\n        electromagnetic field\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonical_momentum" title="Canonical momentum">\n        canonical momentum\n       </a>\n       <b>\n        P\n       </b>\n       (derived from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lagrangian_mechanics" title="Lagrangian mechanics">\n        Lagrangian\n       </a>\n       for this system) is not\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauge_invariant" title="Gauge invariant">\n        gauge invariant\n       </a>\n       . As a consequence, the canonical angular momentum\n       <b>\n        L\n       </b>\n       =\n       <b>\n        r\n       </b>\n       \xc3\x97\n       <b>\n        P\n       </b>\n       is not gauge invariant either. Instead, the momentum that is physical, the so-called\n       <i>\n        kinetic momentum\n       </i>\n       (used throughout this article), is (in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI_units" title="SI units">\n        SI units\n       </a>\n       )\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow {v} =\\mathbf {P} -e\\mathbf {A} }\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="\\mathbf {p} =m\\mathbf {v} =\\mathbf {P} -e\\mathbf {A} width:18.998ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where\n       <i>\n        e\n       </i>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_charge" title="Electric charge">\n        electric charge\n       </a>\n       of the particle and\n       <b>\n        A\n       </b>\n       the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnetic_vector_potential" title="Magnetic vector potential">\n        magnetic vector potential\n       </a>\n       of the electromagnetic field. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Gauge_theory" title="Gauge theory">\n        gauge-invariant\n       </a>\n       angular momentum, that is\n       <i>\n        kinetic angular momentum\n       </i>\n       , is given by\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n   <mi>\n               t\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {S} (\\mathbf {r} ,t)=\\epsilon _{0}c^{2}\\mathbf {E} (\\mathbf {r} ,t)\\times \\mathbf {B} (\\mathbf {r} ,t).}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {S} (\\mathbf {r} ,t)=\\epsilon _{0}c^{2}\\mathbf {E} (\\mathbf {r} ,t)\\times \\mathbf {B} (\\mathbf {r} ,t).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a1def5c88bdb99e90ec83e577815c9a68fdf6b4e" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:30.398ex; height:3.176ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The angular momentum density vector\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               L\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo stretchy="false">\n              (\n             </mo>\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               r\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n             <mo>\n              ,\n             </mo>\n             <mi>\n              t\n             </mi>\n             <mo stretchy="false">\n              )\n             </mo>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} (\\mathbf {r} ,t)}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} (\\mathbf {r} ,t)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dac2bad85a420ba827c3449d04bfd020224dacad" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.456ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       is given by a vector product as in classical mechanics:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Okulov2008J_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Okulov2008J-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                L\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                r\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               t\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                r\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               \xc3\x97\n               <!-- \xc3\x97 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                S\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                r\n               </mi>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               t\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} (\\mathbf {r} ,t)=\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {S} (\\mathbf {r} ,t).}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle \\mathbf {L} (\\mathbf {r} ,t)=\\mathbf {r} \\times \\mathbf {S} (\\mathbf {r} ,t).}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d9f27863b4969ddd4058a037822bd0033ad8de30" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:20.519ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The above identities are valid\n       <i>\n        locally\n       </i>\n       , i.e. in each space point\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="bold">\n               r\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle \\mathbf {r} }\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="\\mathbf {r} " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/eca0f46511c4c986c48b254073732c0bd98ae0c1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.113ex; height:1.676ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       in a given moment\n       <span class="mwe-math-element">\n        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n         <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n          <semantics>\n           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi>\n               t\n              </mi>\n             </mrow>\n            </mstyle>\n           </mrow>\n           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n            {\\displaystyle {t}}\n           </annotation>\n          </semantics>\n         </math>\n        </span>\n        <img alt="{t}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7d4d02c98c6d06946ec61cacc21c08b5ab2eb5e9" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.85ex; height:2.009ex;"/>\n       </span>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">\n        Newton\n       </a>\n       , in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philosophiae_Naturalis_Principia_Mathematica" title="Philosophiae Naturalis Principia Mathematica">\n        <i>\n         Principia\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , hinted at angular momentum in his examples of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion" title="Newton\'s laws of motion">\n        First Law of Motion\n       </a>\n       ,\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         A top, whose parts by their cohesion are perpetually drawn aside from rectilinear motions, does not cease its rotation, otherwise than as it is retarded by the air. The greater bodies of the planets and comets, meeting with less resistance in more free spaces, preserve their motions both progressive and circular for a much longer time.\n        </i>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n         <a href="#cite_note-35">\n          [35]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       He did not further investigate angular momentum directly in the\n       <i>\n        Principia\n       </i>\n       ,\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         From such kind of reflexions also sometimes arise the circular motions of bodies about their own centres. But these are cases which I do not consider in what follows; and it would be too tedious to demonstrate every particular that relates to this subject.\n        </i>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n         <a href="#cite_note-36">\n          [36]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       However, his geometric proof of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion#Second_law" title="Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion">\n        Law of Areas\n       </a>\n       is an outstanding example of Newton\'s genius, and indirectly proves angular momentum conservation in the case of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_force" title="Central force">\n        central force\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Law_of_Areas">\n        The Law of Areas\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: The Law of Areas">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Classical_central-force_problem" title="Classical central-force problem">\n        Classical central-force problem\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Areal_velocity" title="Areal velocity">\n        Areal velocity\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Newton\'s_derivation">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Newton.27s_derivation">\n        Newton\'s derivation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Newton\'s derivation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:258px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newton_area_law_derivation.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="256" data-file-width="256" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/73/Newton_area_law_derivation.gif" width="256"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         Newton\'s derivation of the area law using geometric means.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As a\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planet\n       </a>\n       orbits the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">\n        Sun\n       </a>\n       , the line between the Sun and the planet sweeps out equal areas in equal intervals of time. This had been known since\n       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">\n        Kepler\n       </a>\n       expounded his\n       <a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion" title="Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion">\n        Second Law of Planetary Motion\n       </a>\n       . Newton derived a unique geometric proof, and went on to show that the attractive force of the Sun\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">\n        gravity\n       </a>\n       was the cause of all of Kepler\'s laws.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the first interval of time, an object is in motion from point\n       <b>\n        A\n       </b>\n       to point\n       <b>\n        B\n       </b>\n       . Undisturbed, it would continue to point\n       <b>\n        c\n       </b>\n       during the second interval. When the object arrives at\n       <b>\n        B\n       </b>\n       , it receives an impulse directed toward point\n       <b>\n        S\n       </b>\n       . The impulse gives it a small added velocity toward\n       <b>\n        S\n       </b>\n       , such that if this were its only velocity, it would move from\n       <b>\n        B\n       </b>\n       to\n       <b>\n        V\n       </b>\n       during the second interval. By the\n       <a href="/wiki/Parallelogram_of_force" title="Parallelogram of force">\n        rules of velocity composition\n       </a>\n       , these two velocities add, and point\n       <b>\n        C\n       </b>\n       is found by construction of parallelogram\n       <b>\n        BcCV\n       </b>\n       . Thus the object\'s path is deflected by the impulse so that it arrives at point\n       <b>\n        C\n       </b>\n       at the end of the second interval. Because the triangles\n       <b>\n        SBc\n       </b>\n       and\n       <b>\n        SBC\n       </b>\n       have the same base\n       <b>\n        SB\n       </b>\n       and the same height\n       <b>\n        Bc\n       </b>\n       or\n       <b>\n        VC\n       </b>\n       , they have the same area. By symmetry, triangle\n       <b>\n        SBc\n       </b>\n       also has the same area as triangle\n       <b>\n        SAB\n       </b>\n       , therefore the object has swept out equal areas\n       <b>\n        SAB\n       </b>\n       and\n       <b>\n        SBC\n       </b>\n       in equal times.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At point\n       <b>\n        C\n       </b>\n       , the object receives another impulse toward\n       <b>\n        S\n       </b>\n       , again deflecting its path during the third interval from\n       <b>\n        d\n       </b>\n       to\n       <b>\n        D\n       </b>\n       . Thus it continues to\n       <b>\n        E\n       </b>\n       and beyond, the triangles\n       <b>\n        SAB\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <b>\n        SBc\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <b>\n        SBC\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <b>\n        SCd\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <b>\n        SCD\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <b>\n        SDe\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <b>\n        SDE\n       </b>\n       all having the same area. Allowing the time intervals to become ever smaller, the path\n       <b>\n        ABCDE\n       </b>\n       approaches indefinitely close to a continuous curve.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Note that because this derivation is geometric, and no specific force is applied, it proves a more general law than Kepler\'s Second Law of Planetary Motion. It shows that the Law of Areas applies to any central force, attractive or repulsive, continuous or non-continuous, or zero.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conservation_of_angular_momentum_in_the_Law_of_Areas">\n        Conservation of angular momentum in the Law of Areas\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Conservation of angular momentum in the Law of Areas">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The proportionality of angular momentum to the area swept out by a moving object can be understood by realizing that the bases of the triangles, that is, the lines from\n       <b>\n        S\n       </b>\n       to the object, are equivalent to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum#Scalar_.E2.80.93_angular_momentum_in_two_dimensions" title="Angular momentum">\n        radius\n        <span class="texhtml">\n         <var>\n          r\n         </var>\n        </span>\n       </a>\n       , and that the heights of the triangles are proportional to the perpendicular component of\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum#Scalar_.E2.80.93_angular_momentum_in_two_dimensions" title="Angular momentum">\n        velocity\n        <span class="texhtml">\n         <var>\n          v\n         </var>\n         <sub>\n          \xe2\x8a\xa5\n         </sub>\n        </span>\n       </a>\n       . Hence, if the area swept per unit time is constant, then by the triangular area formula\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">\n         <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">\n          1\n         </span>\n         <span class="visualhide">\n          /\n         </span>\n         <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">\n          2\n         </span>\n        </span>\n        (base)(height)\n       </span>\n       , the product\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        (base)(height)\n       </span>\n       and therefore the product\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        <var>\n         rv\n        </var>\n        <sub>\n         \xe2\x8a\xa5\n        </sub>\n       </span>\n       are constant: if\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        <var>\n         r\n        </var>\n       </span>\n       and the base length are decreased,\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        <var>\n         v\n        </var>\n        <sub>\n         \xe2\x8a\xa5\n        </sub>\n       </span>\n       and height must increase proportionally. Mass is constant, therefore\n       <a href="/wiki/Angular_momentum#Scalar_.E2.80.93_angular_momentum_in_two_dimensions" title="Angular momentum">\n        angular momentum\n        <span class="texhtml">\n         <var>\n          rmv\n         </var>\n         <sub>\n          \xe2\x8a\xa5\n         </sub>\n        </span>\n       </a>\n       is conserved by this exchange of distance and velocity.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the case of triangle\n       <b>\n        SBC\n       </b>\n       , area is equal to\n       <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">\n         1\n        </span>\n        <span class="visualhide">\n         /\n        </span>\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">\n         2\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       (\n       <b>\n        SB\n       </b>\n       )(\n       <b>\n        VC\n       </b>\n       ). Wherever\n       <b>\n        C\n       </b>\n       is eventually located due to the impulse applied at\n       <b>\n        B\n       </b>\n       , the product (\n       <b>\n        SB\n       </b>\n       )(\n       <b>\n        VC\n       </b>\n       ), and therefore\n       <span class="texhtml">\n        <var>\n         rmv\n        </var>\n        <sub>\n         \xe2\x8a\xa5\n        </sub>\n       </span>\n       remain constant. Similarly so for each of the triangles.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="After_Newton">\n        After Newton\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: After Newton">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Leonhard_Euler" title="Leonhard Euler">\n        Leonhard Euler\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bernoulli" title="Daniel Bernoulli">\n        Daniel Bernoulli\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Patrick_d%27Arcy" title="Patrick d\'Arcy">\n        Patrick d\'Arcy\n       </a>\n       all understood angular momentum in terms of conservation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Areal_velocity" title="Areal velocity">\n        areal velocity\n       </a>\n       , a result of their analysis of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion#Second_law" title="Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion">\n        Kepler\'s Second Law\n       </a>\n       of planetary motion. It is unlikely that they realized the implications for ordinary rotating matter.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1736 Euler, like Newton, touched on some of the equations of angular momentum in his\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mechanica" title="Mechanica">\n         Mechanica\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       without further developing them.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Bernoulli wrote in a 1744 letter of a "moment of rotational motion", possibly the first conception of angular momentum as we now understand it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1799,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Simon_Laplace" title="Pierre-Simon Laplace">\n        Pierre-Simon Laplace\n       </a>\n       first realized that a fixed plane was associated with rotation \xe2\x80\x94 his\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Invariable_plane" title="Invariable plane">\n         invariable plane\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Poinsot" title="Louis Poinsot">\n        Louis Poinsot\n       </a>\n       in 1803 began representing rotations as a line segment perpendicular to the rotation, and elaborated on the "conservation of moments".\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1852\n       <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Foucault" title="L\xc3\xa9on Foucault">\n        L\xc3\xa9on Foucault\n       </a>\n       used a\n       <a href="/wiki/Gyroscope" title="Gyroscope">\n        gyroscope\n       </a>\n       in an experiment to display the Earth\'s rotation.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/William_John_Macquorn_Rankine" title="William John Macquorn Rankine">\n        William J. M. Rankine\'s\n       </a>\n       1858\n       <i>\n        Manual of Applied Mechanics\n       </i>\n       defined angular momentum in the modern sense for the first time:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         ...a line whose length is proportional to the magnitude of the angular momentum, and whose direction is perpendicular to the plane of motion of the body and of the fixed point, and such, that when the motion of the body is viewed from the extremity of the line, the radius-vector of the body seems to have right-handed rotation.\n        </i>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       In an 1872 edition of the same book, Rankine stated that "The term\n       <i>\n        angular momentum\n       </i>\n       was introduced by Mr. Hayward,"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       probably referring to R.B. Hayward\'s article\n       <i>\n        On a Direct Method of estimating Velocities, Accelerations, and all similar Quantities with respect to Axes moveable in any manner in Space with Applications,\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayward_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hayward-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which was introduced in 1856, and published in 1864. Rankine was mistaken, as numerous publications feature the term starting in the late 18th to early 19th centuries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, Hayward\'s article apparently was the first use of the term and the concept seen by much of the English-speaking world. Before this, angular momentum was typically referred to as "momentum of rotation" in English.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angular_momentum&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2"
